            </a><a href="/en-us/blog/businessinsights/" title="Business Insights" class="tw-relative tw-mr-4 tw-text-center tw-text-xs tw-font-bold tw-uppercase tw-text-[#7e8b9f] after:tw-absolute after:tw-left-0 after:tw--bottom-2 after:tw-block after:tw-h-[1px] after:tw-w-0 after:tw-bg-[#7e8b9f] after:tw-transition-all after:tw-duration-300 after:tw-ease-in-out hover:after:tw-w-full sm:tw-text-left md:tw-text-sm router-link-active">Business Insights
            </a><!----></div> <div class="tw-flex tw-w-6/12 tw-items-center tw-justify-end sm:tw-w-4/12"><a aria-label="show rss feed" title="show rss feed" lg:tw-flex"><div class="tw-mx-auto lg:tw-w-2/3"><div class="tw-mb-2 tw-items-center sm:tw-flex"><div class="tw-mb-2.5 tw-flex tw-flex-wrap tw-items-center tw-text-xs tw-font-bold tw-uppercase tw-text-[#608DFF] !tw-mb-0"><a href="/en-us/blog/businessinsights/tag/threat-research" title="Threat Research" class="tw-relative tw-mr-4 after:tw-absolute after:tw-top-0 after:tw-bottom-0 after:tw--right-2.5 after:tw-m-auto after:tw-mr-0 after:tw-block after:tw-h-1 after:tw-w-1 after:tw-rounded-full after:tw-bg-current last:tw-mr-0 last:after:tw-hidden ">Threat Research
      </a><a href="/en-us/blog/businessinsights/tag/cybersecurity-awareness" title="Cybersecurity Awareness" class="tw-relative tw-mr-4 after:tw-absolute after:tw-top-0 after:tw-bottom-0 after:tw--right-2.5 after:tw-m-auto after:tw-mr-0 after:tw-block after:tw-h-1 after:tw-w-1 after:tw-rounded-full after:tw-bg-current last:tw-mr-0 last:after:tw-hidden ">Cybersecurity Awareness
      </a><a href="/en-us/blog/businessinsights/tag/managed-detection-and-response" title="Managed Detection and Response" class="tw-relative tw-mr-4 after:tw-absolute after:tw-top-0 after:tw-bottom-0 after:tw--right-2.5 after:tw-m-auto after:tw-mr-0 after:tw-block after:tw-h-1 after:tw-w-1 after:tw-rounded-full after:tw-bg-current last:tw-mr-0 last:after:tw-hidden ">Managed Detection and Response
      </a> <!----></div> <div class="tw-mt-2.5 tw-flex tw-flex-wrap tw-items-center tw-text-sm !tw-mt-0"><!----> <div><!----> <!----></div> <div class="tw-relative tw-ml-5 tw-flex tw-items-center before:tw-absolute before:tw-top-0 before:tw-bottom-0 before:tw--left-3 before:tw-m-auto before:tw-block before:tw-h-1 before:tw-w-1 before:tw-rounded-full before:tw-bg-[#7c7c7c] sm:first:before:tw-hidden"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="14" height="14" viewBox="0 0 23 23" overflow="visible" class="tw-text-[#7c7c7c]"><path d="M11.5 2c5.2 0 9.5 4.3 9.5 9.5S16.7 21 11.5 21 2 16.7 2 11.5 6.3 2 11.5 2m0-2C5.1 0 0 5.1 0 11.5S5.1 23 11.5 23 23 17.9 23 11.5 17.9 0 11.5 0z" style="fill: currentColor"></path> <path d="M11.5 6.6v4.5M12 12.1l3.5 3.2" class="st0"></path></svg> <span class="tw-pl-2">
            21 min read
         </span></div> <div class="tw-relative tw-ml-5 before:tw-absolute before:tw-top-0 before:tw-bottom-0 before:tw--left-3 before:tw-m-auto before:tw-block before:tw-h-1 before:tw-w-1 before:tw-rounded-full before:tw-bg-[#7c7c7c]"><button aria-label="add to bookmark" class="tw-block tw-text-base"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="20" viewBox="0 0 50.9 52.1" overflow="visible" class="tw-w-[1em] tw-h-[1em]"><path d="M3.4 2.5h34.3c.4 0 .7.4.7.8v45.2c0 .6-.6.9-.9.5L21.1 37.3c-.4-.3-.8-.3-1.2 0L3.4 49.5c-.4.4-.9.1-.9-.5l.2-45.7c0-.4.3-.8.7-.8z" fill="#fff" stroke="#adb5b9" stroke-width="5" stroke-miterlimit="10"></path></svg> <!----></button></div></div></div> <h1 class="tw-text-3xl tw-font-bold md:tw-text-4xl md:tw-leading-tight xl:tw-text-5xl xl:tw-leading-tight">
               Deep Dive into the Elephant Framework – A New Cyber Threat in Ukraine
            </h1> <div class="tw-mt-3 tw-items-center tw-text-sm sm:tw-flex"><div class="sm:tw-w-1/3"><div class="tw-mt-2.5 tw-flex tw-flex-wrap tw-items-center tw-text-sm"><a href="/en-us/blog/businessinsights/author/martin-zugec" title="Martin Zugec" class="tw-overflow-hidden tw-rounded-full tw-h-11 tw-w-11"><img width="50" height="50" alt="Martin Zugec" title="Martin Zugec" data-src="https://businessresources.bitdefender.com/hubfs/IMG_6622.jpg" class="tw-h-full tw-w-full tw-object-cover"></a> <div class="tw-pl-2"><div><a href="/en-us/blog/businessinsights/author/martin-zugec" title="Martin Zugec" class="tw-mr-1.5 last:tw-mr-0">Martin Zugec
         </a></div> <p class="tw-text-[#41485e]">
         April 25, 2022
      </p></div> <!----> <!----></div></div> <div class="tw-mt-4 sm:tw-mt-0 sm:tw-w-2/3"><!----></div></div> <picture class="tw-my-6"><source data-not-lazy="" media="(max-width: 600px)" data-srcset="https://businessresources.bitdefender.com/hubfs/Elephant_Martin-1.png"> <source data-not-lazy="" media="(min-width: 701px)" data-srcset="https://businessresources.bitdefender.com/hubfs/Elephant_Martin-1.png"> <img data-not-lazy="" data-src="https://businessresources.bitdefender.com/hubfs/Elephant_Martin-1.png" alt="Deep Dive into the Elephant Framework – A New Cyber Threat in Ukraine" title="Deep Dive into the Elephant Framework – A New Cyber Threat in Ukraine" width="600" height="400" src="https://businessresources.bitdefender.com/hubfs/Elephant_Martin-1.png" class="tw-my-4 tw-w-full"></picture> <div class="content tw-mb-12 tw-text-lg tw-text-black"><p><span data-contrast="auto">At the beginning of the invasion of Ukraine, we released a </span><a href="/blog/businessinsights/security-advisory-a-risk-based-approach-for-improving-your-cybersecurity-posture-due-to-the-invasion-of-ukraine" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><span data-contrast="none">security advisory</span></a><span data-contrast="auto"> with recommendations based on different risk tiers. Since then, our </span><a href="https://www.bitdefender.com/blog/labs/" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><span data-contrast="none">Threat Intelligence (TI)</span></a><span data-contrast="auto"> and </span><a href="https://www.bitdefender.com/business/enterprise-products/managed-detection-response-service.html" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><span data-contrast="none">Managed Detection and Response (MDR)</span></a><span data-contrast="auto"> teams have been actively monitoring the situation and identifying active threats. Not surprisingly, the highest risk group contains businesses and organizations located in Ukraine, especially government entities and critical infrastructure.</span></p>
<!--more-->
<p><span data-contrast="auto">One of the groups actively engaged in pro-Russian cyber-attacks is </span><strong><span data-contrast="auto">UAC-0056. </span></strong><span data-contrast="auto">This group has been active since at least March 2021, and its primary objective seems to be cyber espionage with a focus on key state sectors. Other names for this group are Lorec53, UNC2589, EmberBear, LorecBear, BleedingBear, SaintBear, and TA471.</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">This group has been associated with attacks using OutSteel and GraphSteel stealers (malicious software designed to steal data). OutSteel was written in the AutoIt language, while GraphSteel was written in the Go language (often referred to as Golang). While both languages are known for their ease of use, AutoIt is a simpler language often used by system administrators and scripters. The behavior of Go-based GraphSteel is also more sophisticated – while its primary purpose is harvesting credentials, it is also trying to exfiltrate the most common archives and Office formats like </span><code><span data-contrast="auto" style="background-color: #cccccc;">.docx</span></code><span data-contrast="auto"> or </span><code><span data-contrast="auto" style="background-color: #cccccc;">.xlsx</span></code><span data-contrast="auto"> and locate sensitive files like </span><code><span data-contrast="auto" style="background-color: #cccccc;">.ssh</span></code><span data-contrast="auto">, </span><code><span data-contrast="auto" style="background-color: #cccccc;">.crt</span></code><span data-contrast="auto">, </span><code><span data-contrast="auto" style="background-color: #cccccc;">.key</span></code><span data-contrast="auto">, </span><code><span data-contrast="auto" style="background-color: #cccccc;">.ovpn</span></code><span data-contrast="auto">, or </span><code><span data-contrast="auto" style="background-color: #cccccc;">.json</span></code><span data-contrast="auto">. </span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">Due to the inclusion of media files with extensions like </span><code><span data-contrast="auto" style="background-color: #cccccc;">.jpg</span></code><span data-contrast="auto">, </span><code><span data-contrast="auto" style="background-color: #cccccc;">.png</span></code><span data-contrast="auto">, </span><code><span data-contrast="auto" style="background-color: #cccccc;">.gif</span></code><span data-contrast="auto">, </span><span style="background-color: #cccccc;"><code>.webp</code></span><span data-contrast="auto">, </span><code><span data-contrast="auto" style="background-color: #cccccc;">.avi</span></code><span data-contrast="auto">, </span><span style="background-color: #cccccc;"><code>.mkv</code></span><span data-contrast="auto">, </span><code><span data-contrast="auto" style="background-color: #cccccc;">.mpg</span></code><span data-contrast="auto">, </span><span style="background-color: #cccccc;"><code>.mpeg</code></span><span data-contrast="auto">, and </span><span style="background-color: #cccccc;"><code>.3gp</code></span><span data-contrast="auto">, GraphSteel limits its searches to files that are 50 MB or smaller. While there are certain similarities between OutSteel and GraphSteel, there is not a clear connection between them currently. </span><a href="https://cert.gov.ua/article/37704" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank"><span>The original announcement</span></a><span data-contrast="auto"> by the Computer Emergency Response Team of Ukraine (CERT-UA) regarding GraphSteel indicates an average level of certainty for attribution to UAC-0056.</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">For the rest of this report, we will focus on attacks involving the use of GraphSteel malware. GraphSteel is part of the Elephant Framework – a collection of tools also written in the Go language and deployed in a recent wave of <a href="https://www.bitdefender.com/business/infozone/what-is-phishing.html" rel="noopener">phishing attacks</a> on </span><code><span data-contrast="auto" style="background-color: #cccccc;">.gov.ua</span></code><span data-contrast="auto"> targets. Recently, three different attacks have been observed which relied on the Elephant Framework:</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></p>
<ul>
<li data-leveltext="-" data-font="Calibri" data-listid="6" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="0" data-aria-level="1"><span data-contrast="auto">February 11</span><span data-contrast="auto">th</span><span data-contrast="auto">, 2022 – SentinelOne </span><a href="https://www.sentinelone.com/blog/threat-actor-uac-0056-targeting-ukraine-with-fake-translation-software/" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank"><span data-contrast="none">detected</span></a><span data-contrast="auto"> an attack with fake dictionary software</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></li>
<li data-leveltext="-" data-font="Calibri" data-listid="6" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="0" data-aria-level="1"><span data-contrast="auto">March 11</span><span data-contrast="auto">th</span><span data-contrast="auto">, 2022 – CERT-UA </span><a href="https://cert.gov.ua/article/37704" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank"><span data-contrast="none">reported</span></a><span data-contrast="auto"> an attack with fake antivirus software</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></li>
<li data-leveltext="-" data-font="Calibri" data-listid="6" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="0" data-aria-level="1"><span data-contrast="auto">March 28</span><span data-contrast="auto">th</span><span data-contrast="auto">, 2022 – CERT-UA </span><a href="https://cert.gov.ua/article/38374" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank"><span data-contrast="none">reported</span></a><span data-contrast="auto"> an attack with an “Unpaid wages” email subject</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></li>
</ul>
<h2><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}"><span data-contrast="none" xml:lang="EN-US" lang="EN-US">Anatomy of an Attack</span></span></h2>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">In all known Elephant Framework attacks, the <a href="https://www.bitdefender.com/business/infozone/what-is-spear-phishing.html" rel="noopener">spear-phishing</a> tactic was used for initial compromise. The group demonstrated a good knowledge of social engineering techniques, with emails originating from spoofed Ukrainian email addresses. Email subject and body would often use trending themes (COVID) or use official-looking text.</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">In one of the emails, the threat actor included recommendations for effective security controls after warning about intensified computer attacks by the Russian Federation, including recommendations to use email and web traffic filtering, avoid the use of 3</span><span data-contrast="auto">rd</span><span data-contrast="auto"> party DNS servers, and provide a briefing to employees about possible phishing attacks. This “helpful” email cleverly embedded a link to a malicious payload (masquerading as a recommended antivirus tool).</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">A few different techniques were used to execute the malicious launcher. In this example, the link to the malicious download is included in the body of the email. In other cases, an attached Excel spreadsheet with embedded macros was used.</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></p>
<h3><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}"><span data-contrast="none" xml:lang="EN-US" lang="EN-US">Launcher Component</span></span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}"><span data-contrast="none" xml:lang="EN-US" lang="EN-US"></span></span></h3>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">There are a few different variants of </span><strong><span data-contrast="auto">launchers</span></strong><span data-contrast="auto"> for GraphSteel that we have seen to date. In the case reported by </span><a href="https://www.sentinelone.com/blog/threat-actor-uac-0056-targeting-ukraine-with-fake-translation-software/" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank"><span data-contrast="none">SentinelOne</span></a><span data-contrast="auto">, the downloaded launcher was a Python script converted to an executable (using </span><a href="https://pypi.org/project/pyinstaller/" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank"><span data-contrast="none">pyinstaller</span></a><span data-contrast="auto">). In the other cases, the launcher was written in the Go language like the rest of the Elephant Framework with the launcher’s name varying depending on the attack.</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">Why might threat actors choose the Go language, which is not a mainstream programming language, for this malicious software? Potential reasons include:</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></p>
<ul>
<li data-leveltext="-" data-font="Calibri" data-listid="5" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="0" data-aria-level="1"><span data-contrast="auto">Some security vendors may struggle to detect malware written in the Go language given its less frequent use</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></li>
<li data-leveltext="-" data-font="Calibri" data-listid="5" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="0" data-aria-level="1"><span data-contrast="auto">The payload can be compiled for both Windows and Linux (without code changes)</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></li>
<li data-leveltext="-" data-font="Calibri" data-listid="5" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="0" data-aria-level="1"><span data-contrast="auto">It is easy to use and can be expanded by 3</span><span data-contrast="auto">rd</span><span data-contrast="auto"> party modules</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></li>
</ul>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">After analyzing the GraphSteel code, we identified references to other community modules used by the Elephant Framework; for example, for </span><a href="https://github.com/jcmturner/aescts" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank"><span data-contrast="none">AES cipher</span></a><span data-contrast="auto">, </span><a href="https://github.com/denisbrodbeck/machineid" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank"><span data-contrast="none">generating a unique client ID</span></a><span data-contrast="auto">, or </span><a href="https://github.com/redcode-labs/Coldfire" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank"><span data-contrast="none">Coldfire</span></a><span data-contrast="auto"> (a <a href="https://www.bitdefender.com/business/infozone/what-is-malware.html" rel="noopener">malware</a> development framework for Golang).&nbsp;</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">The launcher does not have the malware payload embedded – instead, it acts as a combination of a downloader and dropper. Upon execution, the launcher connects to the command and control (C&amp;C) server, downloads the malware payload encoded as base64 string, saves it to the local disk and then executes it. The address of the C&amp;C server is hardcoded in this executable and, in all recorded cases, the file dropped by this executable is named </span><code><span data-contrast="auto" style="background-color: #cccccc;">Java-sdk.exe</span></code><span data-contrast="auto">.</span></p>
<h3><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}"><span data-contrast="none" xml:lang="EN-US" lang="EN-US">Downloader Component</span></span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}"><span data-contrast="none" xml:lang="EN-US" lang="EN-US"></span></span></h3>
<p><code><span data-contrast="auto" style="background-color: #cccccc;">Java-sdk.exe</span></code><span data-contrast="auto"> acts as a </span><strong><span data-contrast="auto">downloader</span></strong><span data-contrast="auto"> of the Elephant Framework and, as you probably are expecting by now, is written in the Go language. It uses a similar technique as the launcher – first connecting to a C&amp;C server, then streams a string encoded in base64 which contains the malicious payload, saves it as an executable to disk, and executes it. The address of the C&amp;C server is not embedded – it is provided by the launcher as </span><span data-contrast="auto">a <code><span style="background-color: #cccccc;">base64(AES(&lt;C&amp;C&gt;))</span></code></span><span data-contrast="auto"> argument. Two different malware files are downloaded – GraphSteel (</span><code><span data-contrast="auto" style="background-color: #cccccc;">Microsoft-cortana.exe</span></code><span data-contrast="auto">) and GrimPlant (</span><span style="background-color: #cccccc;"><code>Oracle-java.exe</code></span><span data-contrast="auto">) which are automatically executed. </span><strong><span data-contrast="auto">GrimPlant</span></strong><span data-contrast="auto"> is a relatively simple backdoor that allows remote execution of PowerShell commands. </span><strong><span data-contrast="auto">GraphSteel</span></strong><span data-contrast="auto"> is used for data exfiltration of credentials, certificates, passwords, and other sensitive information.</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">This downloader component is also responsible for establishing persistence by creating a registry value </span><code><span data-contrast="auto" style="background-color: #cccccc;">Java-SDK</span></code><span data-contrast="auto"> under the registry key </span><code><span data-contrast="auto" style="background-color: #cccccc;">HKEY_CURRENT_USER\SOFTWARE\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Run\</span></code><span data-contrast="auto">.&nbsp;</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}"><span data-contrast="auto" xml:lang="EN-US" lang="EN-US"></span><span role="presentation" contenteditable="false"><img alt="Diagram

Description automatically generated" src="https://businessresources.bitdefender.com/hubfs/undefined-Apr-22-2022-02-47-07-32-PM.png" loading="lazy"></span><span data-contrast="auto" xml:lang="EN-US" lang="EN-US"></span></span></p>
<p style="font-size: 14px; text-align: center;"><i><span data-contrast="auto">Typical flow of an attack based on the Elephant Framework</span></i></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">This covers our findings for the initial phase where the Elephant Framework is deployed to the compromised machine. In the next section, we will look in more detail at the core components of the Elephant Framework, GrimPlant and GraphSteel. Both implants are written in the Go language, </span><a href="https://www.intezer.com/blog/research/elephant-malware-targeting-ukrainian-orgs/" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank"><span>comprehensive research</span></a><span data-contrast="auto"> is available from Intezer.</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></p>
<h3 style="font-size: 16px; text-align: left;"><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335551550&quot;:2,&quot;335551620&quot;:2,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}"> <span data-contrast="none" xml:lang="EN-US" lang="EN-US">GrimPlant (Backdoor) Component</span></span></h3>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">GrimPlant’s primary purpose is to allow a threat actor to execute PowerShell commands remotely. The address of the C&amp;C server is provided by </span><code><span data-contrast="auto" style="background-color: #cccccc;">Java-sdk.exe</span></code><span data-contrast="auto"> using the command line parameter </span><code><span data-contrast="auto" style="background-color: #cccccc;">-addr</span></code><span data-contrast="auto">. This address is not provided in plain text, instead, it uses the same </span><code><span data-contrast="auto" style="background-color: #cccccc;">base64(AES(&lt;C&amp;C&gt;))</span></code><span data-contrast="auto"> syntax as the downloader.</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">Communication with the C&amp;C server uses port 80 and is based on </span><a href="https://grpc.io/" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank"><span data-contrast="none">gRPC</span></a><span data-contrast="auto"> – an open-source Remote Procedure Call (RPC) framework, originally designed by Google. The communications are encrypted with TLS, with the certificate hardcoded in the binary.&nbsp;</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">After establishing a connection to the C&amp;C server, GrimPlant sends a heartbeat message every 10 seconds. Included in the heartbeat message is information about the infected endpoint (</span><code><span data-contrast="auto" style="background-color: #cccccc;">uploadSystemInfo</span></code> <span data-contrast="auto">function)</span><span data-contrast="auto">:</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></p>
<ul>
<li data-leveltext="" data-font="Symbol" data-listid="8" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="1" data-aria-level="1"><span data-contrast="auto">Operating System – Hostname, operating system, number of CPUs</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></li>
<li data-leveltext="" data-font="Symbol" data-listid="8" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="2" data-aria-level="1"><span data-contrast="auto">IP Address – Runs a query to </span><code><span data-contrast="auto" style="background-color: #cccccc;">api.ipify.org</span></code><span data-contrast="auto"> to retrieve a public IP address</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}"> <br></span></li>
<li><span data-contrast="auto">User Info – Name, username, HomeDir</span></li>
</ul>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">This malware and its heartbeat message run in an infinite loop, waiting to receive commands from the C&amp;C server and execute them using </span><code><span data-contrast="auto" style="background-color: #cccccc;">PowerShell.exe</span></code><span data-contrast="auto">.</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></p>
<h3><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}"><span data-contrast="none" xml:lang="EN-US" lang="EN-US">GraphSteel (Stealer) Component</span></span></h3>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">GraphSteel’s primary purpose is to exfiltrate data from infected machines. The address of the C&amp;C server is retrieved using the same method as GrimPlant. All communication is encrypted using the AES cipher on port 443. To communicate with the C&amp;C server, it uses WebSockets and the GraphQL query language.</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">Below are the functions used by this malware:</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></p>
<ul>
<li data-leveltext="" data-font="Symbol" data-listid="9" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="1" data-aria-level="1"><strong><span data-contrast="auto">getFileHash()</span></strong><span data-contrast="auto"> – </span><span data-contrast="auto">Checks if the file has been uploaded on the server</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></li>
<li data-leveltext="" data-font="Symbol" data-listid="9" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="2" data-aria-level="1"><strong><span data-contrast="auto">getPublicKey() </span></strong><span data-contrast="auto">–</span> <span data-contrast="auto">Generates a random public key and receives a secret used to derive an AES key for subsequent communication</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></li>
<li data-leveltext="" data-font="Symbol" data-listid="9" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="3" data-aria-level="1"><strong><span data-contrast="auto">uploadChunk() – </span></strong><span data-contrast="auto">Uploads</span> <span data-contrast="auto">files in chunks</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></li>
<li data-leveltext="" data-font="Symbol" data-listid="9" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="4" data-aria-level="1"><strong><span data-contrast="auto">ping() – </span></strong><span data-contrast="auto">Sends client ID to the C&amp;C server</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></li>
<li data-leveltext="" data-font="Symbol" data-listid="9" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="5" data-aria-level="1"><strong><span data-contrast="auto">uploadSystemInfo() –</span></strong><span data-contrast="auto"> Uploads information about the infected machine. Same implementation as GrimPlant</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></li>
<li><strong><span data-contrast="auto">uploadCredentials() –</span></strong><span data-contrast="auto"> Uploads credentials harvested from an infected machine</span></li>
</ul>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">The malware runs two routines to communicate with the C&amp;C server:</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></p>
<ul>
<li data-leveltext="-" data-font="Calibri" data-listid="5" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="0" data-aria-level="1"><span data-contrast="auto">Heartbeat every 20 seconds</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></li>
<li data-leveltext="-" data-font="Calibri" data-listid="5" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="0" data-aria-level="1"><span data-contrast="auto">Exfiltration routine every 20 minutes</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></li>
</ul>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">The exfiltration routine:</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></p>
<ul>
<li data-leveltext="-" data-font="Calibri" data-listid="10" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="0" data-aria-level="1"><span style="color: #000000;">Sends information about the infected system using the <code><span style="background-color: #cccccc;">uploadSystemInfo()</span></code> function</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></li>
<li data-leveltext="-" data-font="Calibri" data-listid="10" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="0" data-aria-level="1"><span style="color: #000000;">Exfiltrates files using <code><span style="background-color: #cccccc;">uploadChunk()</span></code> function&nbsp;</span>
<ul>
<li><span style="color: #000000;">Files are exfiltrated from folders <span style="background-color: #cccccc;"><code>Documents</code></span>, <span style="background-color: #cccccc;"><code>Downloads</code></span>, <span style="background-color: #cccccc;"><code>Pictures</code></span>, <code><span style="background-color: #cccccc;">Desktop</span></code> and from all available drives (<span style="background-color: #cccccc;"><code>D:\</code></span> to <span style="background-color: #cccccc;"><code>Z:\</code></span>)&nbsp;</span></li>
<li><span style="color: #000000;">Limited to files that are smaller than 50 MBs and have one of the following extensions: <code><span style="background-color: #cccccc;">.txt, .doc, .xls, .ppt, .docx, .xlsx, .pptx, .ovpn, .ssh, .zip, .rar, .7z, .jpg, .png, .gif, .webp, .avi, .mkv, .mpg, .mpeg, .3gp, .csv, .json, .crt, .key</span></code><br></span></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><span style="color: #000000;">Harvests credentials and exfiltrates them using the <code><span style="background-color: #cccccc;">uploadCredentials()</span></code> function. Credentials and other sensitive information are extracted using different methods and from various locations:</span>
<ul>
<li data-leveltext="o" data-font="Courier New" data-listid="10" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="1" data-aria-level="2"><span data-contrast="auto">Wifi passwords</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></li>
<li data-leveltext="o" data-font="Courier New" data-listid="10" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="2" data-aria-level="2"><span data-contrast="auto">Chrome and Firefox credentials</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></li>
<li data-leveltext="o" data-font="Courier New" data-listid="10" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="3" data-aria-level="2"><span data-contrast="auto">Credentials from the password vault</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></li>
<li data-leveltext="o" data-font="Courier New" data-listid="10" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="4" data-aria-level="2"><span data-contrast="auto">Credentials from Windows Credentials Manager</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></li>
<li data-leveltext="o" data-font="Courier New" data-listid="10" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="5" data-aria-level="2"><span data-contrast="auto">SSH sessions from Putty, Mobaxterm, openSSH, and Filezilla</span><span style="color: #000000;"></span></li>
<li data-leveltext="o" data-font="Courier New" data-listid="10" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="5" data-aria-level="2"><span style="color: #000000;">Thunderbird</span></li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}"> </span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}"></span><span style="color: #000000;">Exfiltration of wifi passwords is done by parsing output from <span style="background-color: #cccccc;"><code>netsh wlan show profiles</code></span>, followed by <code><span data-contrast="auto" style="background-color: #cccccc;">netsh wlan show profile name=&lt;name&gt; key=clear</span></code>.&nbsp;&nbsp;</span>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">Credentials from a password vault are extracted by parsing the output from following PowerShell command: </span><code><span data-contrast="auto" style="background-color: #cccccc;">([void][Windows.Security.Credentials.PasswordVault,Windows.Security.Credentials,ContentType=WindowsRuntime];$vault = New-Object Windows.Security.Credentials.PasswordVault;$vault.RetrieveAll() | % { $_.RetrievePassword();$_} | Select UserName, Resource, Password | Format-Table –HideTableHeaders</span></code><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></p>
<h2><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}"><span data-contrast="none" xml:lang="EN-US" lang="EN-US">When one payload is not enough</span></span></h2>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">The analyzed incidents mentioned in the first section of this article above are based on the Elephant Framework and use the same kill chain, except for an incident involving a faked copy of Bitdefender software. On March 11</span><span data-contrast="auto">th,</span><span data-contrast="auto"> 2022, a phishing campaign was reported by </span><a href="https://cert.gov.ua/article/37704" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank"><span data-contrast="none">CERT-UA</span></a><span data-contrast="auto"> that included instructions to download a fake Bitdefender antivirus product.</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}"><span data-contrast="auto" xml:lang="EN-US" lang="EN-US"></span><span role="presentation" contenteditable="false"><img alt="Graphical user interface, text, application

Description automatically generated" src="https://businessresources.bitdefender.com/hubfs/undefined-Apr-22-2022-04-57-17-27-PM.png" loading="lazy"></span><span data-contrast="auto" xml:lang="EN-US" lang="EN-US"></span></span></p>
<p style="font-size: 14px; text-align: center;"><i><span data-contrast="auto">The original phishing email. Source: CERT-UA</span></i><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335551550&quot;:2,&quot;335551620&quot;:2,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">Below is the full text of this phishing email (loosely translated from Ukrainian):</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p><code><span style="background-color: #cccccc;"><i>An increased number of computer attacks on information systems of Ukraine was detected since the beginning of the armed aggression of the Russian Federation.</i>&nbsp;</span></code></p>
<p><code><span style="background-color: #cccccc;"><i>Under the Law of Ukraine "On Protection of Information in Information and Telecommunication Systems" based on the decision of The National Security and Defense Council of Ukraine dated 06.03.2022, the State Service of Special Communications together with the Security Service of Ukraine, with the financial support of the Government of France, are taking measures to strengthen information security.</i>&nbsp;</span></code></p>
<p><code><span style="background-color: #cccccc;"><i>To eliminate threats to the state security of Ukraine and ensure the protection of information resources of authorities, organizations, and institutions of all forms of ownership, the following recommendations must be followed:</i>&nbsp;</span></code></p>
<ul>
<li data-leveltext="" data-font="Symbol" data-listid="7" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="1" data-aria-level="1"><code><span style="background-color: #cccccc;"><i>Install additional critical security updates for the Microsoft Windows operating system with a pre-installed certified antivirus available for download from the official Bitdefender website;</i>&nbsp;</span></code></li>
<li data-leveltext="" data-font="Symbol" data-listid="7" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="2" data-aria-level="1"><code><span style="background-color: #cccccc;"><i>Use SBU-certified up-to-date antivirus on all computers;</i>&nbsp;</span></code></li>
<li data-leveltext="" data-font="Symbol" data-listid="7" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="3" data-aria-level="1"><code><span style="background-color: #cccccc;"><i>Filter incoming e-mails on the e-mail server for the presence of spam messages, as well as e-mails containing attachments of the following types: exe, bat, cpl, dll, jar, msi, scr, etc .;</i>&nbsp;</span></code></li>
<li data-leveltext="" data-font="Symbol" data-listid="7" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="4" data-aria-level="1"><code><span style="background-color: #cccccc;"><i>Filter incoming web traffic using content filters for social networks, entertainment sites, and other potentially dangerous resources;</i>&nbsp;</span></code></li>
<li data-leveltext="" data-font="Symbol" data-listid="7" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="1" data-aria-level="1"><code><span style="background-color: #cccccc;"><i>Brief employees on the possible "phishing" attacks;</i>&nbsp;</span></code></li>
<li data-leveltext="" data-font="Symbol" data-listid="7" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="2" data-aria-level="1"><code><span style="background-color: #cccccc;"><i>Avoid the use of third-party DNS servers;</i>&nbsp;</span></code></li>
<li data-leveltext="" data-font="Symbol" data-listid="7" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="3" data-aria-level="1"><code><span style="background-color: #cccccc;"><i>Familiarize the responsible employees with the provided instructions.</i>&nbsp;</span></code></li>
</ul>
<p><code><span style="background-color: #cccccc;"><i>Responsibility for failure to comply with the above recommendations rests with the authorities, organizations, and institutions of all forms of ownership.&nbsp;</i>&nbsp;</span></code></p>
<p><i><span data-contrast="auto"><code><span style="background-color: #cccccc;">To organize cooperation in the investigation of computer incidents, contact the leading specialist of the State Special Service &lt;REDACTED&gt;</span></code>.</span></i><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">The link to the “official Bitdefender website” points to the domain </span><code><span data-contrast="auto" style="background-color: #cccccc;">forkscenter[.]fr</span></code><span data-contrast="auto">. This phishing site spoofs the website </span><span style="background-color: #cccccc;"><code>bitdefender.fr</code></span><span data-contrast="auto">, a version of the Bitdefender website localized in the French language.</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}"><span data-contrast="auto" xml:lang="EN-US" lang="EN-US"></span><span role="presentation" contenteditable="false"><img src="https://businessresources.bitdefender.com/hubfs/undefined-Apr-22-2022-04-58-56-64-PM.png" loading="lazy"></span><span data-contrast="auto" xml:lang="EN-US" lang="EN-US"></span></span></p>
<p style="font-size: 14px; text-align: center;"><i><span data-contrast="auto">The fake Bitdefender.fr website. Source: CERT-UA</span></i><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335551550&quot;:2,&quot;335551620&quot;:2,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">All links on this fake website are downloads for the malicious file named </span><span style="background-color: #cccccc;"><code>BitdefenderWindowsUpdatePackage.exe</code></span><span data-contrast="auto">. Both France and Bitdefender have publicly declared support for Ukraine, and this may be a reason why UAC-0056 chose this context for their phishing site since this aligns with the focus of the spear-phishing email (i.e., to protect systems further due to the heightened geopolitical environment after the invasion of Ukraine). </span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}"><span data-contrast="auto" xml:lang="EN-US" lang="EN-US"></span><span role="presentation" contenteditable="false"><img alt="Timeline

Description automatically generated" src="https://businessresources.bitdefender.com/hubfs/undefined-Apr-22-2022-05-00-04-10-PM.png" loading="lazy"></span><span data-contrast="auto" xml:lang="EN-US" lang="EN-US"></span></span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">This <a href="https://www.bitdefender.com/business/infozone/what-is-phishing.html" rel="noopener">phishing </a>campaign is also interesting due to a key difference compared to Elephant Framework deployments before and after it. With other campaigns, the file </span><code><span data-contrast="auto" style="background-color: #cccccc;">BitdefenderWindowsUpdatePackage.exe</span></code><span data-contrast="auto"> would have likely been a launcher, only responsible for the initial deployment of Elephant Framework. In this case, a parallel deployment was also triggered with a different payload. The initial executable deployed a Discord downloader, </span><code><span data-contrast="auto" style="background-color: #cccccc;">Alt.exe</span></code><span data-contrast="auto">, which in turn deployed two executables. The first is a familiar Go launcher that deployed the rest of the Elephant Framework as described earlier. The second executable, </span><span style="background-color: #cccccc;"><code>One.exe</code></span><span data-contrast="auto">, is a Cobalt Strike Beacon, which deployed another Discord downloader, </span><span style="background-color: #cccccc;"><code>wisw.exe</code></span><span data-contrast="auto">. Persistence was established by creating a startup link called </span><span style="background-color: #cccccc;"><code>BitdefenderControl.lnk</code></span><span data-contrast="auto">, which executes </span><span style="background-color: #cccccc;"><code>wisw.exe</code></span><span data-contrast="auto">. Finally, the malware downloads another executable, </span><span style="background-color: #cccccc;"><code>cesdf.exe</code></span><span data-contrast="auto">, from Discord. Unfortunately, this file is not available for analysis, as the download server was shut down. While the Elephant Framework deployment used </span><span style="background-color: #cccccc;"><code>hxxp://45[.]84.0.116:443</code></span><span data-contrast="auto"> as the C&amp;C server, the Cobalt Strike deployment used the C&amp;C server located at </span><span style="background-color: #cccccc;"><code>nirsoft[.]me</code></span><span data-contrast="auto">.</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}"><span data-contrast="auto" xml:lang="EN-US" lang="EN-US"></span><span role="presentation" contenteditable="false"><img alt="Diagram

Description automatically generated" src="https://businessresources.bitdefender.com/hubfs/undefined-Apr-22-2022-05-01-58-41-PM.png" loading="lazy"></span><span data-contrast="auto" xml:lang="EN-US" lang="EN-US"></span></span></p>
<p style="font-size: 14px; text-align: center;"><i><span data-contrast="auto">Overview of two parallel deployments associated with the spoofed AV attack</span></i><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335551550&quot;:2,&quot;335551620&quot;:2,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></p>
<h2 style="font-size: 16px; text-align: left;"><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335551550&quot;:2,&quot;335551620&quot;:2,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}"><span data-contrast="none" xml:lang="EN-US" lang="EN-US">Conclusion and Recommendations</span></span></h2>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">The best protection against modern cyber-attacks is a defense-in-depth architecture. Start with reducing your attack surface and employing automated controls to prevent most security incidents. For the few incidents that get through your defenses, you want to lean on security operations, either in-house or through a managed service, and leverage strong detection and response tools.</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto">Integrated reputation services can stop an attack during multiple stages – from an initial phishing email, through the execution of a previously unknown payload, through to the successful compromise and subsequent call home to a C&amp;C server.</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p><a href="https://www.bitdefender.com/oem/threat-intelligence-feeds-services.html" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><span data-contrast="none">Bitdefender Threat Intelligence</span></a><span data-contrast="auto"> (TI) is such a reputation service and can be integrated with your existing security infrastructure using the REST API. The services are platform-independent and compatible with any SIEM, SOAR, or other security tools that support consuming data from 3</span><span data-contrast="auto">rd</span><span data-contrast="auto"> party APIs. For OEM partners looking to license such a solution, we deliver up-to-date, contextual intelligence on URLs, IPs, domains, certificates, files, Command and Control servers, and Advanced Persistent Threats.</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p><span data-contrast="auto"><a href="https://www.bitdefender.com/business/infozone/what-is-threat-intelligence.html" rel="noopener">TI</a> is also featured in our Bitdefender Managed Detection and Response offering. Learn more about <a href="https://www.bitdefender.com/business/enterprise-products/managed-detection-response-service.html" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Bitdefender’s MDR Service</a>, </span><span data-contrast="auto">and get to know the Bitdefender experts who work in our security operations center (SOC)</span><span data-contrast="auto">.</span><span data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</span></p>
<div class="hs-embed-wrapper" data-service="youtube" data-responsive="true" style="position: relative; overflow: hidden; width: 100%; height: auto; padding: 0px; max-width: 1280px; min-width: 256px; display: block; margin: 10px auto;"><div class="hs-embed-content-wrapper"><div style="position: relative; overflow: hidden; max-width: 100%; padding-bottom: 56.25%; margin: 0px;" data-mce-style="position: relative; overflow: hidden; max-width: 100%; padding-bottom: 56.25%; margin: 0px;"><iframe style="position: absolute; top: 0px; left: 0px; width: 100%; height: 100%;" title="YouTube video player" allow="accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture" xml="lang" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/TRp7uLYLGiQ" allowfullscreen data-mce-src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/TRp7uLYLGiQ" data-mce-style="position: absolute; top: 0px; left: 0px; width: 100%; height: 100%;" width="1280" height="720" frameborder="0"></iframe></div></div></div>
<h2><span data-contrast="none" xml:lang="EN-US" lang="EN-US"><span data-ccp-parastyle="heading 2">Indicators of Compromise</span></span></h2>

data-font=\"Calibri\" data-listid=\"6\" aria-setsize=\"-1\" data-aria-posinset=\"0\" data-aria-level=\"1\"\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003EMarch 28\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003Eth\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003E, 2022 – CERT-UA \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fcert.gov.ua\u002Farticle\u002F38374\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"none\"\u003Ereported\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003E an attack with an “Unpaid wages” email subject\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan data-ccp-props=\"{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}\"\u003E&nbsp;\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\n\u003Ch2\u003E\u003Cspan data-ccp-props=\"{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}\"\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"none\" xml:lang=\"EN-US\" lang=\"EN-US\"\u003EAnatomy of an Attack\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003EIn all known Elephant Framework attacks, the \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.bitdefender.com\u002Fbusiness\u002Finfozone\u002Fwhat-is-spear-phishing.html\" rel=\"noopener\"\u003Espear-phishing\u003C\u002Fa\u003E tactic was used for initial compromise. The group demonstrated a good knowledge of social engineering techniques, with emails originating from spoofed Ukrainian email addresses. Email subject and body would often use trending themes (COVID) or use official-looking text.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan data-ccp-props=\"{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}\"\u003E&nbsp;\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003EIn one of the emails, the threat actor included recommendations for effective security controls after warning about intensified computer attacks by the Russian Federation, including recommendations to use email and web traffic filtering, avoid the use of 3\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003Erd\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003E party DNS servers, and provide a briefing to employees about possible phishing attacks. This “helpful” email cleverly embedded a link to a malicious payload (masquerading as a recommended antivirus tool).\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan data-ccp-props=\"{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}\"\u003E&nbsp;\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003EA few different techniques were used to execute the malicious launcher. In this example, the link to the malicious download is included in the body of the email. In other cases, an attached Excel spreadsheet with embedded macros was used.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan data-ccp-props=\"{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}\"\u003E&nbsp;\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Ch3\u003E\u003Cspan data-ccp-props=\"{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}\"\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"none\" xml:lang=\"EN-US\" lang=\"EN-US\"\u003ELauncher Component\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan data-ccp-props=\"{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}\"\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"none\" xml:lang=\"EN-US\" lang=\"EN-US\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003EThere are a few different variants of \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003Elaunchers\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003E for GraphSteel that we have seen to date. In the case reported by \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.sentinelone.com\u002Fblog\u002Fthreat-actor-uac-0056-targeting-ukraine-with-fake-translation-software\u002F\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"none\"\u003ESentinelOne\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003E, the downloaded launcher was a Python script converted to an executable (using \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpypi.org\u002Fproject\u002Fpyinstaller\u002F\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"none\"\u003Epyinstaller\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003E). In the other cases, the launcher was written in the Go language like the rest of the Elephant Framework with the launcher’s name varying depending on the attack.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan data-ccp-props=\"{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}\"\u003E&nbsp;\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003EWhy might threat actors choose the Go language, which is not a mainstream programming language, for this malicious software? Potential reasons include:\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan data-ccp-props=\"{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}\"\u003E&nbsp;\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli data-leveltext=\"-\" data-font=\"Calibri\" data-listid=\"5\" aria-setsize=\"-1\" data-aria-posinset=\"0\" data-aria-level=\"1\"\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003ESome security vendors may struggle to detect malware written in the Go language given its less frequent use\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan data-ccp-props=\"{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}\"\u003E&nbsp;\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli data-leveltext=\"-\" data-font=\"Calibri\" data-listid=\"5\" aria-setsize=\"-1\" data-aria-posinset=\"0\" data-aria-level=\"1\"\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003EThe payload can be compiled for both Windows and Linux (without code changes)\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan data-ccp-props=\"{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}\"\u003E&nbsp;\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli data-leveltext=\"-\" data-font=\"Calibri\" data-listid=\"5\" aria-setsize=\"-1\" data-aria-posinset=\"0\" data-aria-level=\"1\"\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003EIt is easy to use and can be expanded by 3\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003Erd\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003E party modules\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan data-ccp-props=\"{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}\"\u003E&nbsp;\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003EAfter analyzing the GraphSteel code, we identified references to other community modules used by the Elephant Framework; for example, for \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fgithub.com\u002Fjcmturner\u002Faescts\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"none\"\u003EAES cipher\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003E, \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fgithub.com\u002Fdenisbrodbeck\u002Fmachineid\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"none\"\u003Egenerating a unique client ID\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003E, or \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fgithub.com\u002Fredcode-labs\u002FColdfire\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"none\"\u003EColdfire\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003E (a \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.bitdefender.com\u002Fbusiness\u002Finfozone\u002Fwhat-is-malware.html\" rel=\"noopener\"\u003Emalware\u003C\u002Fa\u003E development framework for Golang).&nbsp;\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan data-ccp-props=\"{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}\"\u003E&nbsp;\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003EThe launcher does not have the malware payload embedded – instead, it acts as a combination of a downloader and dropper. Upon execution, the launcher connects to the command and control (C&amp;C) server, downloads the malware payload encoded as base64 string, saves it to the local disk and then executes it. The address of the C&amp;C server is hardcoded in this executable and, in all recorded cases, the file dropped by this executable is named \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Ccode\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\" style=\"background-color: #cccccc;\"\u003EJava-sdk.exe\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003E.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Ch3\u003E\u003Cspan data-ccp-props=\"{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}\"\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"none\" xml:lang=\"EN-US\" lang=\"EN-US\"\u003EDownloader Component\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan data-ccp-props=\"{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}\"\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"none\" xml:lang=\"EN-US\" lang=\"EN-US\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ccode\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\" style=\"background-color: #cccccc;\"\u003EJava-sdk.exe\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003E acts as a \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003Edownloader\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003E of the Elephant Framework and, as you probably are expecting by now, is written in the Go language. It uses a similar technique as the launcher – first connecting to a C&amp;C server, then streams a string encoded in base64 which contains the malicious payload, saves it as an executable to disk, and executes it. The address of the C&amp;C server is not embedded – it is provided by the launcher as \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003Ea \u003Ccode\u003E\u003Cspan style=\"background-color: #cccccc;\"\u003Ebase64(AES(&lt;C&amp;C&gt;))\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003E argument. Two different malware files are downloaded – GraphSteel (\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Ccode\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\" style=\"background-color: #cccccc;\"\u003EMicrosoft-cortana.exe\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003E) and GrimPlant (\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan style=\"background-color: \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003EGrimPlant\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003E is a relatively simple backdoor that allows remote execution of PowerShell commands. \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003EGraphSteel\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003E is used for data exfiltration of credentials, certificates, passwords, and other sensitive information.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan data-ccp-props=\"{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}\"\u003E&nbsp;\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003EThis downloader component is also responsible for establishing persistence by creating a registry value \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Ccode\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\" style=\"background-color: #cccccc;\"\u003EJava-SDK\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003E under the registry key \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Ccode\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\" style=\"background-color: data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003EThis covers our findings for the initial phase where the Elephant Framework is deployed to the compromised machine. In the next section, we will look in more detail at the core components of the Elephant Framework, GrimPlant and GraphSteel. The address of the C&amp;C server is provided by \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Ccode\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\" style=\"background-color: #cccccc;\"\u003EJava-sdk.exe\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003E using the command line parameter \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Ccode\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\" style=\"background-color: #cccccc;\"\u003E-addr\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003E. This address is not provided in plain text, instead, it uses the same \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Ccode\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\" style=\"background-color: #cccccc;\"\u003Ebase64(AES(&lt;C&amp;C&gt;))\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003E syntax as the downloader.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan data-ccp-props=\"{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}\"\u003E&nbsp;\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003ECommunication with the C&amp;C server uses port 80 and is based on \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fgrpc.io\u002F\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"none\"\u003EgRPC\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003E – an open-source Remote Procedure Call (RPC) framework, originally designed by Google. The communications are encrypted with TLS, with the certificate hardcoded in the binary.&nbsp;\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan data-ccp-props=\"{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}\"\u003E&nbsp;\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003EAfter establishing a connection to the C&amp;C server, GrimPlant sends a heartbeat message every 10 seconds. Included in the heartbeat message is information about the infected endpoint (\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Ccode\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\" style=\"background-color: data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003E:\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan data-font=\"Symbol\" data-listid=\"8\" aria-setsize=\"-1\" data-aria-posinset=\"1\" data-aria-level=\"1\"\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003EOperating System – Hostname, operating system, data-ccp-props=\"{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}\"\u003E&nbsp;\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli data-leveltext=\"\" data-font=\"Symbol\" data-listid=\"8\" aria-setsize=\"-1\" data-aria-posinset=\"2\" data-aria-level=\"1\"\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003EIP Address – Runs a query to \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Ccode\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\" style=\"background-color: #cccccc;\"\u003Eapi.ipify.org\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003E to retrieve a public IP address\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan data-ccp-props=\"{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}\"\u003E \u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003EUser Info – Name, username, Both France and Bitdefender have publicly declared support for Ukraine, and this may be a reason why UAC-0056 chose this context for their phishing site since this aligns with the focus of the spear-phishing email (i.e., to protect systems further due to the heightened geopolitical environment after the invasion of Ukraine). \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan data-ccp-props=\"{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}\"\u003E&nbsp;\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan data-ccp-props=\"{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}\"\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\" xml:lang=\"EN-US\" lang=\"EN-US\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan role=\"presentation\" contenteditable=\"false\"\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"Timeline\n\nDescription automatically generated\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fbusinessresources.bitdefender.com\u002Fhubfs\u002Fundefined-Apr-22-2022-05-00-04-10-PM.png\" loading=\"lazy\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\" xml:lang=\"EN-US\" lang=\"EN-US\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003EThis \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.bitdefender.com\u002Fbusiness\u002Finfozone\u002Fwhat-is-phishing.html\" rel=\"noopener\"\u003Ephishing \u003C\u002Fa\u003Ecampaign is also interesting due to a key difference compared to Elephant Framework deployments before and after it. With other campaigns, the file \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Ccode\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\" style=\"background-color: #cccccc;\"\u003EBitdefenderWindowsUpdatePackage.exe\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003E would have likely been a launcher, only responsible for the initial deployment of Elephant Framework. In this case, a parallel deployment was also triggered with a different payload. The initial executable deployed a Discord downloader, \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Ccode\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\" style=\"background-color: #cccccc;\"\u003EAlt.exe\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003E, which in turn deployed two executables. The first is a familiar Go launcher that deployed the rest of the Elephant Framework as described earlier. The second executable, \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan style=\"background-color: #cccccc;\"\u003E\u003Ccode\u003EOne.exe\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003E, is a Cobalt Strike Beacon, which deployed another Discord downloader, \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan style=\"background-color: #cccccc;\"\u003E\u003Ccode\u003Ewisw.exe\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003E. Persistence was established by creating a startup link called \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan style=\"background-color: #cccccc;\"\u003E\u003Ccode\u003EBitdefenderControl.lnk\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003E, which executes \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan style=\"background-color: #cccccc;\"\u003E\u003Ccode\u003Ewisw.exe\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003E. Finally, the malware downloads another executable, \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan style=\"background-color: #cccccc;\"\u003E\u003Ccode\u003Ecesdf.exe\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003E, from Discord. Unfortunately, this file is not available for analysis, as the download server was shut down. While the Elephant Framework deployment used \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan style=\"background-color: #cccccc;\"\u003E\u003Ccode\u003Ehxxp:\u002F\u002F45[.]84.0.116:443\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003E as the C&amp;C server, the Cobalt Strike deployment used the C&amp;C server located at \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan style=\"background-color: #cccccc;\"\u003E\u003Ccode\u003Enirsoft[.]me\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003E.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan data-ccp-props=\"{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}\"\u003E&nbsp;\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan data-ccp-props=\"{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}\"\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\" xml:lang=\"EN-US\" lang=\"EN-US\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan role=\"presentation\" contenteditable=\"false\"\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"Diagram\n\nDescription automatically generated\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fbusinessresources.bitdefender.com\u002Fhubfs\u002Fundefined-Apr-22-2022-05-01-58-41-PM.png\" loading=\"lazy\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan data-contrast=\"auto\" xml:lang=\"EN-US\" lang=\"EN-US\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp style=\"font-size: 14px;
